Design Note — Quest Pacing: No NPC dumps their full quest chain at once. Quests are gated by level, season, standing, and prerequisite completion. A player who focuses only on one NPC will hit natural walls that push them toward other characters.

Uncle Bob — Quest Chain (8 Quests)

Bob's quest chain is the backbone of Year 1. It doubles as the game's extended tutorial without ever feeling like one. Each quest teaches a core mechanic through a concrete task Bob needs help with. The player arrives mid-Greening (day 43, Greening 15) when dandelions are blooming, providing a natural nectar flow that eliminates the need for spring feeding. Bob teaches feeding in Fall instead, when the player must spend harvest money to ensure the colony survives winter.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q0: Meet Uncle Bob1Mid-Spring Y1 (Greening)Game start (gatekeeper)Player arrives in Cedar Bend. Go talk to Uncle Bob by his surviving hive. Bob thanks the player for coming, explains his hospital stay, the winter that killed 11 of 12 hives, the importance of the dandelion flow keeping the survivor alive, and teaches basic controls (chest, toolbar, smoker, hive tool, inspection keys, journal). All other quests and daily tasks are suppressed until this is complete.+25 XP. Knowledge Log: "Bee Biology", "Hive Components". Unlocks all subsequent quests and daily tasks.
Q1: First Light1Mid-Spring Y1After Q0Smoke the surviving hive to calm the bees (select smoker, press E), then switch to the hive tool and open it up. Inspect at least 3 frames. Bob: "Now go smoke that hive and take a look inside. I want to know what she's doing in there." Return to Bob afterward.+25 XP. Knowledge Log: "Frame Reading". Return-to-Bob prompt triggers debrief dialogue about the brood pattern and the dandelion flow.
Q2: Reading the Room1Spring Y1After Q1Complete a full independent inspection: check at least 8 frame sides (front and back). Identify brood pattern quality, honey stores, and anything unusual. Bob watches from the tailgate: "I need you to do a thorough inspection this time. Every frame, both sides." Return to Bob with findings.+25 XP. Knowledge Log: "Brood Pattern". Return-to-Bob debrief teaches brood nest shape, population growth on dandelion flow, and introduces the concept of swarming and space management.
Q3: The Girls Are Building1Late Spring Y1After Q2The dandelion flow is filling the brood box. The colony needs more space or they will swarm. Grab a honey super from the storage chest and add it to the hive using Hive Management. Bob: "See how they're building burr comb on top? That's them telling you they need space."+50 XP. Knowledge Log: "When to Add Space". Return-to-Bob debrief introduces clover flow timing and when to expect harvestable honey.
Q4: First Pull1Summer Y1 (Wide-Clover+)After Q3 + month-gated to Wide-Clover (month 2)The clover flow has filled the supers. Select frames with ≥80% capping. Uncap, extract, and bottle the harvest. Return a jar to Bob. He says: "The honey isn't the point. The honey is proof the bees are doing well." Introduces Saturday Market via Frank.+75 XP. Knowledge Log: "Honey Harvest". Return-to-Bob debrief teaches that fall will ask for the harvest back -- the bees need 60 lbs to survive winter, and any shortfall is on the player to make up.
Q5: Battening Down1Fall Y1 (Full-Earth+)After Q4 + month-gated to Full-Earth (month 4)Winter is coming. Do an alcohol wash to check mite levels (under 3 per hundred). Treat with oxalic acid if high. Check honey stores -- if below 60 lbs, buy sugar from Tanner's and install a feeder bucket with 2:1 thick syrup. Bob teaches both fall feeding (2:1 thick syrup for stores) and previews spring feeding for Year 2 (1:1 thin syrup to mimic a nectar flow and get the queen laying). "You'll spend some of your harvest money on feed. That's the cost of keeping bees alive."+100 XP. Knowledge Log: "Winter Prep", "Emergency Feeding". Return-to-Bob debrief covers winter behavior (don't open the hive, check weight, fondant if light) and spring feeding timing for Year 2.
Q6: Lloyd's Lot2Spring Y2After Q5 + Level 2 + survived winterVisit Lloyd Petersen's property with Bob. Walk the site. Pay $200 clearing fee. Clear and prep the apiary site (3 tasks over 1 week). Place first hive at Timber & Woodlot. Bob can't do the work: "My back says I'm sixty-two. My liver says maybe not even that."+100 XP, +40 Standing. Cost: $200. UNLOCKS: Timber & Woodlot Apiary (basswood, tulip poplar, wildflower forage; up to 4 hive slots). Knowledge Log: "Apiary Site Selection".
Q7: Spring Count2–3Spring Y3After Q6 + 2nd winter survivedInspect all hives across both apiaries. Report winter survival rate to Bob. If ≥80% survived: full capstone dialogue. Bob: "I think you know more than I did at this point. Don't tell anyone I said that."+150 XP, +50 Standing. Chain complete. Recurring mentorship visits unlocked (bi-weekly, +20 XP, indefinite). Knowledge Log: "The Mentor's Approval".
Design Note — Bob's Recurring Presence: After the chain completes, Bob doesn't vanish. He remains available for bi-weekly visits (+20–25 XP), appears at the Crossroads Diner on Tuesdays, and has seasonal dialogue that reflects his health and the weather. He stops being the quest driver and becomes the emotional anchor.
Design Note — Year 1 Pacing: The player arrives mid-Greening (day 43) when dandelions are blooming. This prevents dead time at the start of the game. Q0 through Q3 can be completed within the first two weeks. Q4 (First Pull) is month-gated to Wide-Clover, giving the player time to observe the hive develop and learn seasonal rhythms. Q5 (Battening Down) is month-gated to Full-Earth, ensuring the player has harvested before facing winter prep. Month-gated quests that fail their start conditions are automatically retried each new day.

Uncle Bob — Farewell Quest Chain (4 Quests)

These quests trigger in Years 4–5 as Bob's liver failure progresses. They are the emotional climax of the game. Bob doesn't announce he's dying — he just starts putting things in order, and the player realizes what's happening through the accumulation of small, deliberate acts of love.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q9: The Workshop Key3+Late Fall Y4After Q8 + Bob's health visibly decliningBob gives the player the key to his workshop and the combination to the tool cabinet. He walks them through every piece of equipment: what it does, how to maintain it, where the replacement parts are. "I've been collecting this stuff for twenty years. You'll need it longer than that." He gives the player the original smoker — the one Sandy gave him as a gift when he started keeping bees. It is old and dented and works perfectly. Bob says nothing about why he's giving it now.+100 XP, +40 Standing. Full workshop access unlocked. Sandy's Smoker (unique item, +10% calm radius). Knowledge Log: "The Workshop Key."
Q10: The Deed and the Lawyer3+Winter Y4–5After Q9A drive to Albion. At the lawyer's office, Bob updates his will. The property, the hives, and the equipment go to the player. Bob: "The lawyer wanted me to explain why I'm leaving a farm to a kid. I told him you're the only person who earned it."+100 XP, +50 Standing. Deed to Bob's property (transfers ownership after Bob's death). Knowledge Log: "The Deed and the Drive."
Q11: The Rounds4+Spring Y5After Q10Bob asks the player to drive him into town one last time. He visits every person who mattered. He doesn't say goodbye — he says the thing he should have said years ago. At the diner, he tells Rose: "You kept this town fed and you kept me company and I never said thank you properly. So. Thank you." Rose doesn't cry. She cuts him a double slice of pecan pie and sits down across from him and they talk about Sandy for the first time in eight years.+75 XP, +30 Standing. All visited NPCs gain +15 relationship. Knowledge Log: "The Rounds." Triggers Bob's final decline.
Q12: The Last Inspection4+Late Spring Y5After Q11Bob asks the player to help him to the apiary one more time. It is a good day — warm, clear, the kind of day that bees work hard and the air smells like clover. Bob sits in his chair next to the surviving hive — the original hive, the one that started everything. He asks the player to open it. Slowly. Frame by frame. "Tell me what you see." The player describes the colony. Bob listens. He nods. He says: "Good. That's good." They sit together in the apiary until the sun gets low. Bob dies peacefully at home that night.+200 XP, +75 Standing. Knowledge Log: "The Last Inspection." Triggers Telling the Bees quest. Bob's death scene plays (hospice philosophy: peaceful, prepared, surrounded by what mattered).
Design Note — Hospice Philosophy: Bob's death is not a tragedy. It is a good death — anticipated, prepared for, and surrounded by meaning. The farewell quests are Bob putting his affairs in order with dignity, not melodrama. Each quest is an act of love disguised as practical business. The player doesn't save Bob. They honor him by receiving what he's built and continuing it. This is hospice philosophy: a good death is not the absence of death but the presence of everything that mattered.

Telling the Bees — Quest (1 Quest)

The emotional climax of the entire game. This quest triggers immediately after Bob's death and is required before any memorial quests can proceed.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Telling the Bees4+After Bob's deathQ12: The Last Inspection completeDarlene approaches and says: "There's something you need to do before anything else. You need to go tell the bees." She explains the oldest tradition in beekeeping: when a keeper dies, someone goes to the hives and tells them. The player walks the apiary alone. At each hive, they knock on the box and say the words: "Your keeper has died, but you have a new keeper now, and you are not to leave." At the surviving hive — the original, the one that started everything — the player pauses. The bees hum. The moment holds.+100 XP, +50 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Telling the Bees — The Oldest Tradition." All hives gain a subtle visual shimmer for 3 in-game days (the bees heard). Unlocks Bob's Memorial Service quest.
Design Note — Foreshadowing (Three-Beat Structure): "Telling the Bees" is foreshadowed three times before it triggers:
Beat 1 (Year 1): The player finds an old book in Bob's workshop: "The Beekeeper's Companion, 1923 Edition." One chapter is dog-eared: "On the Telling of the Bees." If inspected, the Knowledge Log records: "An old tradition. When a beekeeper dies, someone must tell the bees, or they will leave." Most players will forget this.
Beat 2 (Year 2): At the Long Table dinner, Lloyd tells a story about his grandfather's bees: "When Grandpa Petersen died, my dad went out to every hive that morning before the funeral and knocked on each one and told them. I thought he was crazy. But not a single hive absconded that spring." Played as a charming anecdote. Filed under folklore.
Beat 3 (Year 3): Darlene mentions it directly: "Did Bob ever tell you about telling the bees? It's an old, old thing. Centuries. I've never had to do it. Hope I never do." Said casually. The player has no reason to think it's relevant.
When the moment finally arrives, players who caught the foreshadowing will feel it coming before Darlene speaks. Players who didn't will discover the tradition in the moment and feel the weight of something ancient meeting something personal. Both experiences work. That's the design.

Holiday Quests (4 Quests)

Each of Cedar Bend's four seasonal holidays has an associated quest that deepens the player's connection to the town's traditions. These quests recur annually in simplified form after the first completion.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
The Quickening Gift2+Greening 12 (Spring) Y2+Survived first winterRose asks the player to provide a comb of spring honey for the Quickening Morn breakfast — continuing the tradition Bob started. Bring a frame of fresh comb to the town square at dawn. Help Rose set up the communal table. The whole town tastes the first honey of the year from the player's hive.+50 XP, +25 Standing. "Keeper of the Comb" reputation title. Annual recurring (simplified).
The Beam Day Booth2+High-Sun 19 (Summer) Y2+Market access unlockedFrank offers the player a premium booth at the Founder's Beam all-day market. Set up a display with at least 5 products, including at least one specialty item (infused honey, candles, or lip balm). Engage with 10 customers. Highest single-day sales opportunity in the game.+75 XP, +30 Standing. 2x market day revenue. Summer specialty item demand boost for one month.
The Fire Keeper2+Full-Earth 7 (Fall) Y2+Lloyd relationship ≥20Lloyd asks the player to help gather deadfall from the timber for the Reaping Fire pyre. Spend one day in the timber collecting fallen branches (10 bundles). Deliver to the town square. Help light the fire at dusk. Stay for the stories. Lloyd tells the 1994 storm story. Silas interrupts at the usual point. The player adds a story of their own — about the surviving hive.+50 XP, +25 Standing. +15 lumber from gathering. The player's story becomes part of the annual tradition.
A Place at the Table2+Deepcold 21 (Winter) Y2+Bob relationship ≥40 (Y2–4) or Bob's death (Y5+)Help Bob (Years 2–4) or host independently (Year 5+) the Long Table dinner. Set the table, prepare food (honey-glazed ham recipe from Rose, honey cornbread, mead if available). Invite at least 4 NPCs. Each invited NPC has unique Long Table dialogue that reveals something personal they don't share at other times.+75 XP, +40 Standing. All attending NPCs gain +10 relationship. Unique holiday-only Knowledge Log entries.

Standalone quests that weave the player deeper into Cedar Bend's social fabric. These are not chain-dependent — they trigger based on relationship levels, time, and proximity.

Agnes Pfeiffer — Quest Chain (3 Quests)

Agnes is the generational mirror. Her quests explore the tension between loving where you are and wanting something else — a reflection of the player's own journey in reverse. Agnes was born in Cedar Bend and is looking for her way out; the player came to Cedar Bend and found purpose. Her chain is quiet, character-driven, and ends with real consequences for the diner.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q1: The Study Break2+Any, Y2Visited diner 3 times after 8 PMThe player finds Agnes studying at the counter after close. Textbooks spread out, coffee cold. She is embarrassed — "Don't tell Rose." She asks the player if they have ever felt stuck between loving where you are and wanting something else. A brief, honest conversation. No task, no fetch quest — just a moment of recognition between two people on opposite trajectories.+25 XP, +10 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Night Classes." Agnes's background unlocked in journal.
Q2: The Ride to Waterloo2–3Wednesday, Y3After Q1Agnes's car breaks down on a Wednesday night — class night. The player drives her to Waterloo (45-minute drive each way). During the drive, Agnes talks: grew up in Cedar Bend, father left when she was ten, mother works at the grain elevator. Rose hired her at sixteen. She loves Rose. She loves the diner. She also knows that if she doesn't leave, she'll be pouring coffee at sixty-five. The game's second sustained car-ride conversation (the first is the Deed and the Lawyer with Bob).+50 XP, +15 Standing. Knowledge Log: "The Drive to Waterloo." Agnes friendship deepened.
Q3: The Application3+Any, Y4After Q2Agnes asks the player to look over her UNI scholarship application. The player helps with the essay. Rose finds out Agnes is leaving. A scene at the diner counter — Rose says nothing for a long time, then: "You go. You go and you do it right. And when you're done, there's a booth here with your name on it. That's not an offer. That's a fact." Agnes cries. Rose doesn't. This is Rose passing forward the same grace that Cedar Bend gave the player.+75 XP, +25 Standing. Chain complete. Knowledge Log: "The Application." If Agnes leaves (Y5), Rose hires a new waitress. The diner feels slightly different — a tiny, true detail about how towns change even as they stay the same.

Darlene Kowalski — Quest Chain (10 Quests)

Darlene is the safety net and the standard. Her quests focus on quality, queen management, and the deeper craft. She's visible from the start (fence line neighbor) but her chain activates through observation and need. The chain spans Years 1–5, culminating in a generational handoff as Darlene transitions from teacher to peer.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q1: Over the Fence1Spring Y1NoneVisit Darlene's property. Observe her inspect one of her hives. Answer 3 observation questions correctly (brood pattern, population estimate, queen status). She demonstrates what a healthy, established operation looks like.+50 XP, +20 Standing. Knowledge Log: "What a Healthy Hive Looks Like". Can visit Darlene anytime.
Q2: The Marked Queen1–2Summer Y1After Q1 + spotted queen 3 timesFind and mark the queen in your surviving hive using the international color system. Must complete within a single inspection without losing her. Darlene: "You need to know who's in charge. And more importantly, you need to know when she's been replaced."+75 XP, +25 Standing. Queen marking pen (permanent tool). Knowledge Log: "Queen Identification & Marking".
Q3: When Good Queens Go Bad2Y2 (queen failure event)After Q2 + queen failure in any hiveIdentify the failing/missing queen. Order replacement through Tanner's (or accept from Darlene at standing ≥250). Install new queen. Verify acceptance after 3 days. Darlene: "Every beekeeper loses a queen. It's what you do in the next 48 hours that separates the hobbyists from the beekeepers."+100 XP, +30 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Emergency Requeening". Queen sourcing from Darlene at high relationship.
Q4: Three Hive Walk2–3Spring Y2–Y3After Q3 + managing ≥4 hivesInspect all 3 of Darlene's hives. For each, record: queen status, brood quality, population strength, varroa load estimate, and stores estimate. Correctly identify the best split candidate.+100 XP, +35 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Comparative Hive Assessment". Darlene's advanced queen genetics dialogue.
Q5: The Old Way3–4Y3–Y4After Q4 + Level 3Over 4 inspections across 2 months, evaluate queen performance in 3+ hives using Darlene's observational criteria: brood compactness, pattern consistency, temperament, honey production rate. Rank your queens and present your assessment. Darlene's grandmother's approach before DNA testing existed.+125 XP, +40 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Observational Queen Assessment". Preferred queen traits visible in inspection UI.
Q6: Passing It Forward4Y4+After Q5 + Level 4 + queen rearing unlockedGraft queen cells from Darlene's best colony. Raise a mated queen. Install her in one of Darlene's hives. Darlene: "I can't do the grafting anymore. My hands aren't steady enough. But you can." Her grandmother's genetic line continues through Eli.+150 XP, +60 Standing. Emergency queen sourcing from Darlene at no cost (once per season). Darlene's queen line available for grafting (premium genetics). Knowledge Log: "The Legacy of a Line".
Q7: Darlene's Story4Y4+After Q6 + Darlene relationship ≥60Invite Darlene to coffee at the diner. She shares the full story of learning beekeeping from her grandmother in 1976 — the smoker lessons, the first sting, the queen that lived eleven years. The first time she opens up completely. Rose brings pie without being asked. Darlene: "My grandmother never called herself a beekeeper. She said she was a bee-listener. She said the bees will tell you everything if you stop talking long enough to hear it."+100 XP, +40 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Darlene's Grandmother — The Bee Listener". Darlene's family backstory entries unlocked in journal.
Q8: The Third Generation4–5Y4–Y5After Q7Darlene invites Eli to her kitchen to view the family photo album. Three generations of Cedar Bend beekeepers in black-and-white and faded color. Help her identify equipment in the photographs and caption them for preservation. "I need someone who knows what they're looking at. My daughter lives in Minneapolis. She doesn't know a super from a smoker."+75 XP, +30 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Three Generations — A Cedar Bend Beekeeping Album". Historical equipment variants visible in Darlene's property scenes.
Q9: The Last Stand5Y5After Q8 + Darlene relationship ≥80Darlene is scaling down. She asks Eli to help assess her remaining hives — which to keep, which to pass on. Inspect each colony together. Evaluate on genetics, health, and temperament. Accept the colonies she decides to transfer. Darlene: "I kept bees for forty-seven years. That's enough. But these girls — they deserve someone who'll still be climbing ladders next spring."+125 XP, +50 Standing. 2–3 colonies transferred to player (premium genetic stock). Knowledge Log: "Receiving Another Keeper's Bees". Darlene's apiary visually scales down.
Q10: A Cedar Bend Beekeeper5+Y5+After Q9Darlene asks to walk the player's apiary one final time. She inspects with her eyes, not her hands. She asks three knowledge questions — not to test, but to hear the answers spoken aloud by someone she trusts. At the end, she nods. Darlene: "You're not my student anymore. You're not Bob's student anymore. You're a Cedar Bend beekeeper. That's a thing that means something." She goes home. The chain is complete.+200 XP, +75 Standing. Chain complete. Title: "Cedar Bend Beekeeper" (from Darlene). Darlene's queen genetics permanently available. Knowledge Log: "A Cedar Bend Beekeeper". Darlene remains available for seasonal dialogue and emergency advice.

Dr. Ellen Harwick — Milestone Quest Chain (10 Quests)

Ellen is the science. Unlike other NPC chains, her quests trigger by hive count milestones rather than time or events. Each milestone deepens the player's understanding of bee biology, colony health, and research methodology. The chain spans the full game and culminates in the Master Beekeeper certification.

QuestLevelMilestone TriggerPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
M1: The First Hive11st colonized hiveFirst hive establishedVisit the extension office. Dr. Harwick introduces herself and teaches proper smoker technique — not just how to use it, but the science behind why smoke calms bees (disrupts alarm pheromone reception, triggers gorging response). "Most beekeepers smoke their hives because someone told them to. I want you to understand why it works."+50 XP, +15 Standing. Knowledge Log: "The Science of Smoke". Extension office accessible anytime. Dr. Harwick available for consultation.
M2: Colony Dynamics1–22nd colonized hiveAfter M1 + 2 active hivesInspect both hives in the same session. Identify differences in growth rate, temperament, and foraging behavior. Present comparison findings to Dr. Harwick. She explains why genetically identical packages can diverge within weeks. "Two colonies, same package source, same apiary. One's thriving, one's struggling. Why? That's the question that keeps me in this field."+75 XP, +20 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Colony Divergence & Population Dynamics". Comparative inspection notes visible in journal.
M3: Health Monitoring23rd colonized hiveAfter M2 + 3 active hivesLearn the alcohol wash mite counting method from Dr. Harwick. Perform the test on all three hives. Record whether each is above or below the treatment threshold (3 mites per 100 bees). She doesn't sugarcoat it: "Varroa destructor is the single biggest killer of managed honey bee colonies in North America. You need to count them, not guess."+75 XP, +25 Standing. Alcohol wash kit (permanent tool). Mite count tracking in inspection UI. Knowledge Log: "Varroa Threshold Management".
M4: Something Personal2–34th colonized hiveAfter M3 + 4 active hives + all inspected in 1 weekLearn American Foulbrood (AFB) detection and the ropiness test. Dr. Harwick demonstrates with a sample slide, then shares her own story: she lost an entire apiary to AFB in 2003. "Fourteen colonies. Burned every one. You don't forget the smell." The first time the science track gets personal.+100 XP, +30 Standing. AFB detection in inspection UI. Knowledge Log: "American Foulbrood — Detection and Response". Dr. Harwick's field notebook viewable (historical data).
M5: The Special Technique35th colonized hiveAfter M4 + 5 active hives + first harvest completedLearn split-harvest technique: harvest separately by apiary location and bloom timing. Compare honey from different sites — color, aroma, crystallization rate. Dr. Harwick: "Most beekeepers blend everything together. You're past that. Each site has a signature. Learn to read it."+100 XP, +35 Standing. Split-harvest option in extraction UI. Varietal identification enhanced. Knowledge Log: "Terroir in Honey — Site-Specific Harvesting".
M6: The Mentor Gift3–46th colonized hiveAfter M5 + 6 active hives + full season with no lossesDr. Harwick gives the player a Zeiss refractometer — a precision instrument for measuring honey moisture content. It belonged to her graduate advisor at Iowa State. "Dr. Pedersen gave this to me when I finished my dissertation. He said, 'The instrument doesn't make you better. It just proves what your tongue already knew.' Now I'm giving it to you. Same reason."+125 XP, +40 Standing. Zeiss Refractometer (unique item, precise moisture readings to 0.1%). Knowledge Log: "Precision Measurement & Honey Quality". Moisture displayed to one decimal in all harvest results.
M7: Bee Genetics47th colonized hiveAfter M6 + 7 active hives + marked a queen unassistedOne-hour genetics session at the extension office. Dr. Harwick covers Carniolan, Italian, and Buckfast traits — temperament, overwintering ability, honey production, disease resistance. The player agrees to enter colony data in her county research database. "I've been collecting this data for fifteen years. I need beekeepers who keep records, not just bees."+125 XP, +45 Standing. Genetic trait visibility in queen inspection data. Knowledge Log: "Bee Genetics — Subspecies and Selection". County database contributor status.
M8: Colony Collapse Warning48th colonized hiveAfter M7 + 8 active hives + completed varroa treatment cycle with pre/post countsReview Dr. Harwick's 15-year county colony loss map. Compare the player's mite data against regional trends. Designate one colony as a sentinel hive for ongoing monitoring. "The sentinel doesn't get treated. It tells us what's really happening in the field. It's risky — you'll lose the colony if mites spike. But the data helps every beekeeper in Millhaven County."+150 XP, +50 Standing. County mite forecast data in journal. Sentinel monitoring protocol. Knowledge Log: "Sentinel Monitoring & Regional Data".
M9: Life's Research4–59th colonized hiveAfter M8 + 9 active hives + 50+ lbs honey in a seasonSpend a morning at the extension office reviewing Dr. Harwick's 30-year county data binders — colony counts, loss rates, bloom timing shifts, mite resistance trends. She is preparing an unpublished manuscript and offers the player a named contributor credit. "Thirty years of data and I still can't get anyone to publish it. Maybe if a working beekeeper's name is on it, someone will listen."+150 XP, +60 Standing. Named contributor to Dr. Harwick's manuscript. Full county historical data visible in journal. Knowledge Log: "Thirty Years of County Data".
M10: The Beekeeper's Journal510th colonized hiveAfter M9 + 10 active hives + full year of complete inspection recordsDr. Harwick presents her personal field journal, dating to 1994 — every colony she has managed, every loss, every discovery. She asks the player to add the first new entry. Then she administers the Master Beekeeper certification: written knowledge check (15 questions from the Knowledge Log), practical inspection (identify 5 specific conditions), and a season management plan for a 15+ hive operation. "I don't recommend people lightly. You've earned this."+200 XP, +75 Standing. Chain complete. Title: "Certified Master Beekeeper". Dr. Harwick's journal (permanent item). Advanced diagnostic detail permanently in all inspections. Knowledge Log: "Master Certification & The Beekeeper's Journal".
Safety Net -- Dr. Harwick Research Nuc (Winter Workshop S5): If the player begins spring (Quickening Day 1-7) with 0-1 surviving colonized hives, Dr. Harwick offers a subsidized research nuc from her county extension program at $80 (vs. normal $130). She visits the apiary 3-4 times per year to inspect it for research data. Fires once per game. Her periodic visits create natural NPC presence at the apiary and maintain the science relationship even when milestone quests are not active.

Silas Crenshaw (Carpenter) — Quest Chain (BEING REDESIGNED)

Silas is the practical infrastructure NPC. The Honey House is now functional from game start (inherited from Uncle Bob), so Silas's original Q1-Q3 (restoration quests) are deprecated. His chain is being redesigned from "gatekeeper who unlocks the Honey House" to "craftsman who helps you upgrade it." Q4 (The Upgrade) remains as a template for the new chain direction.

Design Note — Silas Redesign: Silas's relationship arc is being reworked. Instead of gating access to the Honey House, he becomes the craftsman who helps you improve it. The emotional core remains: Silas built the original for Bob, and now he helps the player make it their own. His bench for Bob (built without being asked, never acknowledged) anchors the character. The new chain will focus on upgrades (Tiers 1-4) rather than restoration.

Carl Tanner (Feed & Supply) — Quest Chain (10 Quests)

Carl is the supply backbone. His quests build the player's relationship from walk-in customer to permanent retail partner. He is the first NPC the player interacts with commercially outside of Frank's market, and his store is both the primary source of equipment and a community information hub through the bulletin board.

Safety Net -- Carl's Tab (Winter Workshop S5): If the player's cash drops below $50 during spring (Quickening through Greening), Carl offers $150 credit at Tanner's: "Your uncle was good for it." Repay by end of High-Sun (Day 112) or take -5 Standing. This prevents soft-locking when a player survives winter with no cash and needs supplies to restart. Carl's gesture is both gameplay safety net and character moment -- he is extending trust the way small-town shopkeepers do.

Help Carl coordinate the alternative sourcing.+75 XP, +25 Standing. Alternative treatment source permanently available. Knowledge Log: "Supply Chain Resilience". Carl's Columbus distributor connection unlocked for future orders.
Q5: Custom Order2Y2After Q4Carl establishes a custom order system for specialty equipment not normally in stock. Place the first order (5–7 day delivery, no markup on items under $40). After 3 custom orders, the most-requested items get permanently stocked. Carl: "If you're ordering it, someone else wants it too. Tell me what to carry."+50 XP, +20 Standing. Custom ordering available permanently. High-frequency items added to regular stock after 3 orders. Knowledge Log: "The Custom Order Book".
Q6: The Broken Extractor2–3Y2–Y3After Q5 + Honey House builtCarl has a broken 9-frame radial extractor in the back storage — it belonged to a beekeeper who moved out of county. Motor's dead, but the drum is perfect. He offers it at scrap price if Eli can fix it. Diagnose the motor fault (burned winding) and install a replacement part ordered through Carl. "I can't sell something broken. But if you fix it, that's your extractor for what it cost me to store it."+100 XP, +30 Standing. 9-frame radial extractor (major upgrade from 2-frame hand crank). Knowledge Log: "Equipment Repair — The Extractor". Repair skill unlocked for future equipment maintenance.
Q7: Bee Package Day1–2Spring (any year)After Q2 + first spring in store42 bee packages arrive Thursday at 7 AM. Carl needs help coordinating distribution to 16 customers who pre-ordered. Help unload, organize by name, and answer questions from nervous first-time beekeepers. One package is damaged; handle the triage. Carl: "This is the biggest day of my year. Forty-two boxes of bees, sixteen customers, and half of them have never seen a package before. I need another set of hands."+75 XP, +25 Standing. First pick of any unclaimed packages (if available). Community reputation boost (+5 relationship with any customer present). Knowledge Log: "Package Day — The Supply Side".
Q8: The Seasonal Display2–3Spring Y2–Y3After Q7 + Standing ≥200Carl wants a beekeeping equipment display in the front store window to attract new customers during spring. Help design and set up the display using authentic gear from the player's collection: a frame of drawn comb, a smoker, veil, hive tool, and a jar of honey. Carl: "People walk by and see feed bags. I want them to see something alive."+75 XP, +25 Standing. Store window display drives new customers (increased foot traffic, potential new beekeepers in county). Knowledge Log: "Merchandising & Education".
Q9: The Old Supply Ledger3–4Y3–Y4After Q8 + Carl relationship ≥60Carl discovers his grandfather's 1952 beekeeping supply ledger in the back office. Review it together — prices, product names, suppliers that no longer exist. Identify how equipment has evolved over seventy years. "Granddad sold a smoker for $1.75 in 1952. Same model costs forty-two dollars now. But the bees haven't changed a bit."+100 XP, +35 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Seventy Years of Beekeeping Supply". Historical equipment knowledge unlocked (trivia and context in inspection notes).
Q10: Tanner's Honey Corner3–4Y3–Y4After Q9 + Standing ≥400Carl permanently assigns the back-left corner of the store for the player's beekeeping equipment and honey display. A dedicated retail presence: honey varietals, beeswax products, candles, and educational signage. Carl: "Your uncle had a corner in this store for twenty years. Wasn't official — he just kept showing up with things worth selling. Now it's official." He hangs a hand-painted sign: "[Player's Farm Name] Honey & Bee Products."+125 XP, +50 Standing. Chain complete. UNLOCKS: Tanner's Honey Corner (permanent retail presence, expanded product display, passive daily income). Winter catalog pre-order available. Wholesale pricing permanent. Knowledge Log: "Two Shelves, Two Markets". Carl remains the primary vendor with full wholesale access.
Design Note — Carl's Role: Carl is the quiet economic partner who complements Frank. Frank is the public-facing market relationship; Carl is the supply-side relationship. Together they form the two pillars of the player's commercial life. Carl's expanded chain adds depth through practical problem-solving (backorders, equipment repair, custom orders) and community events (Bee Package Day, the seasonal display). The Old Supply Ledger quest grounds the store in history, and Tanner's Honey Corner makes the player's presence in the store permanent. Carl's store also serves as an information hub through the bulletin board — a natural way to surface community events and seasonal tips without a quest tracker or notification system.

Rose Delacroix (Diner Owner) — Quest Chain (10 Quests)

Rose is the heart of Cedar Bend. Her quests build from casual customer to honey supplier to permanent fixture in the town's daily rhythm. The diner is already a functional location for energy recovery; Rose's chain layers narrative and economic meaning onto a space the player already visits regularly. The later quests make the player's honey — and by extension, the player — part of Cedar Bend's identity.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q1: Honey in the Coffee2AnyDiner Regular status (4 visits) + first harvestThe player brings their own honey to the diner and uses it in their coffee. Rose notices. She comes out of the kitchen to sit across from Eli at the counter. "Bob talked about you. Said you had the hands for it. Let me taste that." She samples it for kitchen use — the beginning of a business relationship built on breakfast.+50 XP, +15 Standing. Rose comments on the honey's flavor profile (teaches terroir). Diner meals cost $1 less permanently. Knowledge Log: "The Taste of a Place".
Q2: The Daily Special2AnyAfter Q1 + delivered 3 jars totalRose needs 8 jars of consistent honey before Friday for a menu feature — honey butter with biscuits, honey-drizzled cornbread, and sweet tea. A time-pressure quest that teaches reliability. Rose: "People order the same thing every day for twenty years. You give them something new that's also local? They talk about it."+75 XP, +25 Standing. UNLOCKS: Diner honey contract (2 jars/week ongoing, guaranteed purchase at market price + 10%). Rose puts "Honey from [Player's Farm Name]" on the chalkboard menu. Knowledge Log: "Farm-to-Table".
Q3: Honey Butter2–3AnyAfter Q2 + buckwheat honey availableRose requests buckwheat honey specifically for her grandmother's honey butter recipe. The first varietal-specific order — flavor matters, not just quantity. "My mother's honey butter was dark. Rich. Like molasses had a better idea of itself. That's what I need." The player must produce or source buckwheat honey from the right apiary site.+75 XP, +25 Standing. Rose's Honey Butter added to diner menu (+$3/week royalty). Knowledge Log: "Varietal Flavor Profiles". Rose friendship level 2.
Q4: The Chalkboard2–3AnyAfter Q3Rose creates a permanent chalkboard feature for local honey on the menu. She asks the player to provide a proper brand name and description for the display. Design the label identity (dialogue choices for name style: farm-forward, varietal-forward, or place-forward). Rose writes it on the board herself. "If it's going on my wall, it's going to sound like something worth tasting."+50 XP, +20 Standing. Branded presence on diner chalkboard (visible to all NPCs). Player's honey identity established in-game. Knowledge Log: "Building a Brand".
Q5: The Short-Handed Morning2–3AnyAfter Q4 + Rose relationship ≥40Agnes is absent (car trouble or class conflict). Rose asks the player to help with the breakfast rush. Serve 5 tables in a timing minigame — take orders, deliver plates, refill coffee. Not a honey quest. A community quest that builds the player's place in the diner's daily rhythm. Rose: "I've run this place alone before. I just don't like to."+75 XP, +25 Standing. All diner NPCs gain +5 relationship (they saw the player working). Diner energy recovery bonus (+10% for one week). Knowledge Log: "The Breakfast Shift".
Q6: The Wildflower Order3AnyAfter Q5 + multiple apiary sites activeRose requests light, floral honey that "tastes of Iowa fields." Not buckwheat, not linden — wildflower. A quality-focused quest requiring the right apiary site (River Bottom or Rowland Farm edges) and careful harvest timing. "I don't want sweet. I want a jar that tastes like driving past a meadow with the windows down."+100 XP, +30 Standing. Premium wildflower honey contract (+15% over standard pricing). Rose friendship level 3. Knowledge Log: "Terroir — The Meadow Jar".
Q7: The Beeswax Candles3FallAfter Q6 + beeswax crafting unlockedRose orders 12 real beeswax taper candles for the diner's Christmas table settings. A crafting quest that expands the player's product line beyond honey. "Every December my mother put real candles on the tables. Not paraffin. Real beeswax. They smell like summer in the middle of winter. I want that back."+75 XP, +25 Standing. Beeswax candle recipe added to crafting menu. Annual candle order from Rose (recurring seasonal income). Knowledge Log: "Beeswax Craft — Beyond Honey".
Q8: Cedar Bend Honey Pie3–4AnyAfter Q7 + 2 distinct honey varietals availableRose develops a signature recipe requiring both light and dark honey simultaneously — wildflower for the filling, buckwheat for the glaze. The player must provide two distinct batches from different apiary sites. Visit the kitchen to watch her bake. Taste-test together. "My mother made pies for forty years. I want to make one she couldn't."+100 XP, +30 Standing. "Cedar Bend Honey Pie" added to diner menu (generates +$5/week passive income royalty). Knowledge Log: "Collaboration — The Signature Recipe".
Q9: The County Food Festival3–4SummerAfter Q8 + Frank Q5 (County Fair) availableRose enters her Cedar Bend Honey Pie in the county food festival. The player gets credit if it places — recognition that the honey is as much a part of the recipe as the baking. If it wins, Rose hangs the ribbon in the diner window. "That's not my ribbon. That's our ribbon. Half of that pie is your bees."+100 XP, +35 Standing. Variable competition rewards. Diner foot traffic increase (+10% for one season). Knowledge Log: "County Recognition". Rose friendship max level.
Q10: The Honey Wall4AnyAfter Q9 + 3+ distinct honey varietals produced over careerRose displays one jar of every honey varietal the player has produced on the diner's back wall — a permanent, visible record of seasons, sites, and blooms. Each jar has a hand-written label in Rose's handwriting: the varietal, the year, and the apiary. Rose: "People walk in and see the pie case. I want them to turn around and see what goes into it. Every season you've kept bees in Cedar Bend, right there on the wall."+150 XP, +50 Standing. Chain complete. UNLOCKS: The Honey Wall (permanent diner display, visual record of player's beekeeping career). Rose becomes a vocal advocate (+2/week passive Standing). All diner NPCs have expanded dialogue. Knowledge Log: "The Honey Wall — A Record of Seasons".
Design Note — Rose and Community: Rose's expanded chain is deliberately the most emotionally grounded. She is not a quest-giver in the traditional sense — she is a person who notices, who invites, who includes. The early quests build a supplier relationship (honey in the coffee, daily specials, varietal orders). The mid-chain quests deepen it into community (working the breakfast rush, the wildflower order, beeswax candles). The late quests create permanence: the signature honey pie, the county festival entry, and the Honey Wall that displays every varietal the player has produced. By Q10, the diner is not just the player's social anchor — it is a public record of their entire beekeeping career.

June Wellman (Postmaster) — Quest Chain (10 Quests)

June is the quiet observer and the literal point of connection between Cedar Bend and the outside world. Her quests range from practical (shipping bees, ordering supplies, tracking packages) to deeply emotional (Bob's letter, the photograph after his death). The post office is already a functional stop for mail-order packages; June's chain gives it narrative weight and makes June the quiet archivist of Cedar Bend's most important moments.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q1: The Buzzing Box1–2Spring Y1First bee package ordered (mail order)Pick up the first mail-order bee package from the post office. June has it behind the counter — she has heard it buzzing since 6 AM. She handles it with professional calm but admits: "My grandma did this for thirty-one years and said she never got used to the bee days. Your uncle used to pick his up with bare hands. I'm not there yet." She explains the mail-order process and timing for future orders.+25 XP, +10 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Mail-Order Bees — How They Travel". June's post office schedule and package tracking available.
Q2: Handle With Care1–2AnyAfter Q1A bee package arrives damaged from the distribution center — crushed corner, some dead bees visible through the screen. June kept it warm behind the counter and called as soon as it arrived. "I didn't know what else to do. The box was making sounds I've never heard a box make." Perform emergency assessment: check queen cage, estimate surviving population, install what's left. A lesson in triage.+50 XP, +15 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Emergency Package Assessment". June flags future damaged shipments immediately (faster notification).
Q3: Catalog Season1–2AnyAfter Q2 + 4 post office visitsJune introduces the catalog system. Dadant, Mann Lake, Brushy Mountain — the supply chains behind the hobby. She keeps a stack of catalogs behind the counter and knows when orders typically ship. "Most people don't think about how their equipment gets here. It starts with a truck in Wisconsin and ends with me hauling a 40-pound box to the counter." Unlock mail-order equipment suppliers.+50 XP, +15 Standing. Equipment catalog ordering available. Knowledge Log: "The Supply Chain — Wisconsin to Cedar Bend". Order tracking in journal.
Q4: The Lost Order1–2AnyAfter Q3A queen shipment goes missing. The tracking number shows it left the breeder but never arrived at the regional hub. June investigates — calls the distribution center, checks the routing, traces the package. She needs the player to check with Carl (in case it was misdelivered to the store) and ask Frank (who had a queen order the same week). Track it across multiple NPCs. June finds it: mislabeled, sitting in a Des Moines sorting facility. She gets it rerouted. "This is why I don't take vacation during queen season."+75 XP, +20 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Postal Logistics & Live Shipments". June's tracking accuracy improved (lost orders become rarer). All signing NPCs gain +5 relationship.
Q5: Rural Route 42AnyAfter Q4 + Standing ≥150June discovers abandoned hives on Rural Route 4 during her mail route. She recognizes them as beehives because of Eli. "There are three white boxes sitting behind a barn on the Pryce property. Harlan Pryce died two years ago. I don't think anyone's touched them since." Investigate the site: assess hive condition, determine if any colonies survived, and legally claim salvageable equipment. A glimpse into what happens to an apiary when the beekeeper is gone.+75 XP, +25 Standing. Salvaged equipment (frames, boxes, possibly a surviving colony). Knowledge Log: "Abandoned Apiaries — Harlan Pryce's Legacy". June gains deeper dialogue about the history of Cedar Bend's beekeepers.
Q6: The Sticky Letter2AnyAfter Q5A honey jar the player shipped breaks in transit and the recipient complains. June handles it professionally but teaches the player about postal shipping limitations for food products. "Glass jars and the US mail have an adversarial relationship. Let me show you how your uncle used to pack them." Learn proper packaging technique and send a replacement. A small quest about doing right by your product and your customers.+50 XP, +15 Standing. Honey shipping supplies available at post office. Proper packaging technique reduces future breakage to zero. Knowledge Log: "Shipping Honey — The Postal Way".
Q7: Swarm in the Mailbox2Spring/SummerAfter Q6 + swarm season activeA swarm clusters in the post office's rural delivery mailbox. June can't deliver mail. She calls Eli. "There are ten thousand bees in my mailbox and Mrs. Patterson wants her seed catalog." Capture and relocate the swarm to the player's apiary. The whole town watches. Beekeeping as community service.+75 XP, +25 Standing. Free colony (captured swarm). Community reputation boost (+5 relationship with all NPCs in town center). Knowledge Log: "Swarm Capture — Community Service".
Q8: Special Delivery2AnyAfter Q7 + Dr. Harwick M3 completedDr. Harwick has a rare queen specimen box shipped to the post office — temperature-sensitive, held specifically for in-person pickup. June contacts the player: "Dr. Harwick said you'd know what to do with this. She said it needs to be at her office within two hours of pickup. I'm holding it behind the counter in a warm spot." Collect the box and deliver it to the extension office. Connects June's chain to the Harwick milestone track.+50 XP, +15 Standing. Knowledge Log: "Temperature-Sensitive Shipments". Dr. Harwick relationship +10. Cross-chain connection established.
Q9: June's Garden2–3SpringAfter Q8 + June relationship ≥50June wants to plant a pollinator garden behind the post office. She has been reading about it since she started handling bee packages. "If I'm going to be the person who ships bees, I should probably help feed them too." Help select plants (lavender, echinacea, black-eyed Susan, bee balm), plant them together, and observe the bloom throughout the season. A small, quiet investment in the town's ecology.+75 XP, +25 Standing. Pollinator garden established (minor forage bonus for home apiary). June gains seasonal garden dialogue. Knowledge Log: "Urban Pollinator Habitat". June friendship max level.
Q10: The Annual Report3–4Y4+After Q9 + 4 full years of post office ordersJune pulls out four years of shipping records — every bee package, every queen, every catalog order, every jar shipped out. She has kept a tally. "I wanted to show you something. This is every package I've handled for you since the first buzzing box." Review the history together: how the operation grew from one nervous package to dozens of shipments per season. Provide honey varietals for her desk display — a jar from each year, each site. June: "My grandmother had a picture of Bob and Sandy on her desk for thirty years. I'm going to have your honey."+100 XP, +40 Standing. Chain complete. Knowledge Log: "Four Years in Packages — The Postal Record". Package delivery speed improved (orders arrive 1 day faster). June remains the post office NPC with expanded seasonal dialogue and deepened community role. Knowledge Log: "The Post Office Stands".
Design Note — June's Emotional Weight: June's expanded chain transforms the post office from a package pickup location into a narrative anchor. The early quests (damaged packages, lost orders, catalog ordering) build practical familiarity. The mid-chain quests (Rural Route 4, swarm capture, Special Delivery) connect June to the wider community and other NPC chains. The later quests (June's garden, the annual report) create emotional investment. And after Bob's death, June delivers the photograph — making her the keeper of three artifacts: the letter (still delivered through story events), the knowledge that the letter existed, and the photograph. She is the quiet archivist of Cedar Bend's most important moments.

Lloyd Petersen (Woodlot Manager) — Quest Chain (4 Quests)

Lloyd is the land. His quests are the most environmentally grounded in the game — focused on understanding forests as living systems and the relationship between trees and bees. His chain begins through Uncle Bob's introduction and gates the Timber & Woodlot's deeper potential.

QuestLevelSeasonPrerequisitesObjectiveRewards
Q1: The Walk2Spring Y2Bob Q7 (Lloyd's Lot) completedReturn to the Timber alone. Lloyd meets Eli at the trailhead. Walk the full 80 acres together. Lloyd identifies 8 tree species and their value to bees: linden (the crown jewel), black locust (early nectar), tulip poplar, wild cherry, maple, willow, hickory, and oak (pollen only). He quizzes Eli on 3 identifications. Lloyd: "A forest isn't lumber. A forest is a calendar. Every tree blooms on its own schedule, and if you read it right, your bees never go hungry."+75 XP, +20 Standing. Knowledge Log: "The Timber — A Forager's Calendar". Tree species overlay visible in Timber scene (subtle leaf icons marking identified species). Forage calendar for Timber apiary unlocked in journal.
Q2: The Linden Season2–3Summer Y2 (Wide-Clover)After Q1 + hives placed at TimberLloyd invites Eli to observe the linden bloom — the two-week window when the entire canopy is covered in flowers and the Timber becomes the most productive forage zone in the game. Monitor hive weight daily for 14 days using the hive scale (or manual lift-check). Record the nectar flow peak. Lloyd: "Two weeks. That's all the lindens give you. But those two weeks make the whole year."+100 XP, +30 Standing. Knowledge Log: "The Linden Flow". Linden honey identified as a distinct varietal in the grading system (premium pricing at market). Timber hive productivity bonus during linden bloom permanently visible in forecasts.
Q3: Clearing and Planting3Fall Y2–Spring Y3After Q2Lloyd shows Eli a section of the timber where diseased ash trees need to be removed. Help Lloyd clear the dead trees (3 work sessions, 15 energy each). In spring, plant replacement saplings: 4 linden and 2 black locust. Lloyd provides the seedlings. "You take out the dead wood and put in something that feeds the next generation. That's forestry. That's beekeeping too, if you think about it."+100 XP, +35 Standing. Cost: 45 energy total across 3 sessions. Timber apiary expanded to 6 hive slots (up from 4). Planted trees begin growing (visible each year, productive by Year 5). 15 lumber harvested from cleared trees. Knowledge Log: "Sustainable Forestry".
Q4: Co-Steward3–4Y3–Y4After Q3 + Level 3 + Standing ≥400Lloyd is getting older. He offers Eli a formal co-stewardship arrangement: shared management of the timber in exchange for maintaining the trails, monitoring tree health, and keeping the apiary productive. No money changes hands — it is a handshake agreement between two people who understand the land. Lloyd: "I'm not selling it and I'm not leaving it. But I need someone who'll walk it when I can't. Bob said you were that person. I believe him now."+150 XP, +50 Standing. Chain complete. UNLOCKS: Timber co-stewardship (no seasonal fee, permanent access, expanded to 8 hive slots, lumber harvesting rights). Lloyd remains available for seasonal dialogue about tree health and forest management. Knowledge Log: "Stewardship".
Design Note — Lloyd and Long-Term Investment: Lloyd's chain is the most patient in the game. The trees planted in Q3 do not become productive until Year 5 — an investment the player may not see pay off within a single playthrough's most active years. This is intentional: it teaches the real-world lesson that forestry operates on a longer timeline than annual crops. The co-stewardship offer in Q4 is the game's clearest statement about legacy — what you build outlasts you.

No quest chain exists in isolation. Cross-NPC dependencies encourage engagement with the full cast without forced branching.
